    <credit-words default-x="84.7458" default-y="2286.62" font-size="12" justify="left" valign="top" />
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words>There is a problem in the original Whistling edition</credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words>of 1843 (reprinted by Edition Peters in 1890), at </credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words>measure 60.  See the piano RH notes in the upper </credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words>image, where the note values for beat 6 do not add up</credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words>correctly.</credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words />

    <credit-words> </credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words>Our solution for this transcription was to use 16</credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words>th</credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words> notes </credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words>(semiquavers) for the final two notes of the piano RH.</credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words>This allows these final notes to fall on beat 6 of the </credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words>measure, which is presumably the intention of the </credit-words>
    <credit-words />
    <credit-words>composer.</credit-words>
